        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68002409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer273101396392824528">Books where people die are very hard for me to read about. But those are also the ones that touch me the most. <br/><br/>Tessa has cancer. She has been fighting cancer for the past 4 years, and now only has months to live. She wants to make the most of the time she has, and so she makes a "Before I Die" list, a list of all the things she wants to do before she dies. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380326733i/691307.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>What would you do? I for one, would probably want to spend all my time with loved ones, although I don’t think you can assume what a person w</span>
  <span id="freeText273101396392824528" style="display:none">Books where people die are very hard for me to read about. But those are also the ones that touch me the most. <br><br>Tessa has cancer. She has been fighting cancer for the past 4 years, and now only has months to live. She wants to make the most of the time she has, and so she makes a "Before I Die" list, a list of all the things she wants to do before she dies. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380326733i/691307.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What would you do? I for one, would probably want to spend all my time with loved ones, although I don’t think you can assume what a person would want in such a time unless it’s actually happening (God forbid).<br><br>Tessa doesn’t play a weepy, whiny character who thinks the world should revolve around her since she’s about to die. In fact, she’s kind of a bitch. She’s blunt, honest, knows what she wants and does anything possible to get it, because, well, life is short. First up is sex, then drugs, shoplifting, fame, love, etc. <br><br>So you all know what will happen in the end. She’ll die. The end, right? What you don’t know is that it’ll break your heart along the way. There are quite a few heartbreaking quotes, but this one touched me the most:<br><br>Tessa’s words to her dad: <i>‘No, then you’ll die. Before me. The way it’s supposed to be.’</i><br><br>Whenever I hear of a child dying anywhere in the world, it always hurts. It’s so sad to think of someone dying before they get to see how wonderful life could be, had they had the time to enjoy it. Tessa tries her best to enjoy whatever time is left. But there’s only so much you can do. She can’t finish school, she can never go to university, so many things that normal teenagers look forward to. She’s just not given a chance. That’s the worst part. When reading, and growing to know Tessa better and liking her, you realize that there’s nothing you can do for her. You’re not going to get a happy ending. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380326733ra/691308.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>...and live.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer265398128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8342336033358550915">I really didn't like this book. It started off okay, but it just got worse and worse. <br/><br/>Tessa has cancer, and is dying. She has a list of things she wants to do before she dies. The list is things like sex, drugs, say yes to everything for a whole day, get famous, nonsense stuff. Then she falls in love with the boy next door. Her list turns into things like hold my brother, kiss my love, have a cup of tea, little things like that. This book could have been really great, if it wasn't for all of the</span>
  <span id="freeText8342336033358550915" style="display:none">I really didn't like this book. It started off okay, but it just got worse and worse. <br /><br />Tessa has cancer, and is dying. She has a list of things she wants to do before she dies. The list is things like sex, drugs, say yes to everything for a whole day, get famous, nonsense stuff. Then she falls in love with the boy next door. Her list turns into things like hold my brother, kiss my love, have a cup of tea, little things like that. This book could have been really great, if it wasn't for all of the sex. This book was just FULL of it, and it was very graphic. I'm sorry, but if I was dying, I wouldn't be thinking about sex all the time. I wouldn't. But throughout the whole book, it is just about sex. Sex, sex and more sex. One part cancer, five thousand parts sex. I may be the only teenager out there who doesn't want to read about sex, but it's true. Book should have more meaning to them, especially when it is about a girl who is dying. I mean, if I wanted to read a book about sex, I would get one of those adult novels, not a bucketlist book. I do like how her list changes to everyday things, but still I feel like it was a waste of a read, and I am forever stuck with the mental images of horrible those sex scenes. Yugh. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14751602533775800792">If you need a reminder of all that's important in this world, then you should read this novel. Even if you don't think so. The title says it all. Narrated by a Tessa, a girl who is dying of cancer, <u>Before I Die</u> gives a realistic portrait of what she wants to accomplish in the little time left to her.<br/><br/>Now please don't think I'm sexist when I say this, but 99% of the women I know make lists.   <span id="freeText14751602533775800792" style="display:none">If you need a reminder of all that's important in this world, then you should read this novel. Even if you don't think so. The title says it all. Narrated by a Tessa, a girl who is dying of cancer, <u>Before I Die</u> gives a realistic portrait of what she wants to accomplish in the little time left to her.<br /><br />Now please don't think I'm sexist when I say this, but 99% of the women I know make lists. It's something I admire about them. Lists—it's a girl thing.<br /><br />Tessa, makes lists. Lists of things she wants to accomplish in the short time she has to live. All I can say is don't get in the way of a girl with a list.<br /><br />There are books that help you think about life in a different way. <u>Before I Die</u> did that for me. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17317477383276853202">I have just finnished this book and I write this review through tears. In the day it took me to read I have laughed, cried, felt uplifted and humbled. <br/><br/>This is the story of 16 year old Tessa who is dying of terminal cancer.   <span id="freeText17317477383276853202" style="display:none">I have just finnished this book and I write this review through tears. In the day it took me to read I have laughed, cried, felt uplifted and humbled. <br /><br />This is the story of 16 year old Tessa who is dying of terminal cancer. In her last months she makes a list of 10 things she wants to do before she dies (this includes falling in love and saying yes to everything for one whole day). Tessa goes through a range of emotions including anger (why her?) but the overriding feeling I got from her was an amazing spirit. She notices things that you and I forget to notice - the colour of leaves, the sound of a thunder storm, sunshine reflecting in a tea cup. These are the things that make her feel alive and she embraces them in a way that most of us who think we have years left infront of us don't. <br /><br />This is a beautifully written and important book. It reminds us to live. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12106452294181639173"><i>Before I Die</i> was so freaking good! <br/><br/>Even though you know beforehand that the MC is going to die, you still wont be prepared for it. Nope, you wont. It's kind of like <i>Me Before You</i> or <i>A Walk to Remeber</i> because you will still end up shedding some tears after finishing the book. Maybe even before you do.   <span id="freeText12106452294181639173" style="display:none"><i>Before I Die</i> was so freaking good! <br /><br />Even though you know beforehand that the MC is going to die, you still wont be prepared for it. Nope, you wont. It's kind of like <i>Me Before You</i> or <i>A Walk to Remeber</i> because you will still end up shedding some tears after finishing the book. Maybe even before you do. Just know, that this book WILL MAKE YOU CRY.<br /><br />This is my first book by Jenny Downham and I'm officially hooked. It was very hard to put this book down and go on with my real life. If I could stay in my reading zone forever and ever I would never be bored or sad. <br /><br />The thing I loved most about this book, or I guess while reading it, was because it made me think of other books/movies/characters. I don't really know how to explain it but I just like when authors or books do that. AS long as I'm always remembering books I like/loved I'm good.<br /><br />I don't want to spoil to much other than the fact that Tessa, who is the MC dies, BUT then again you already know that before you read it. <br /><br />I just want to say that this book broke my heart and everything else. It was so freaking good. I loved every second of it. I can also see myself rereading it over and over again.<br /></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8342077367382869081">I'd heard a little about this book when I started reading it. Not much, but mostly good things. But when I started it, I had no clue what I was in for.<br/><br/>The title makes it clear that the book is about death. Tessa, at sixteen, is about to die. But the book is about so much more than that. It's really about living. Tessa makes a list of 10 things she wants to do before she dies. Each one leads to different, varying consiquences, but they all help her live, just a little.<br/><br/>This book is beautiful and g</span>
  <span id="freeText8342077367382869081" style="display:none">I'd heard a little about this book when I started reading it. Not much, but mostly good things. But when I started it, I had no clue what I was in for.<br /><br />The title makes it clear that the book is about death. Tessa, at sixteen, is about to die. But the book is about so much more than that. It's really about living. Tessa makes a list of 10 things she wants to do before she dies. Each one leads to different, varying consiquences, but they all help her live, just a little.<br /><br />This book is beautiful and gut wrenching. The characters are real and painfully flawed. There are moments when Tessa is selfish and unlikeable, but others when all you want to do is hold her and make her safe. The book deals with a lot of mature subject matter - sex, drugs, teen pregancy - but in a realistic and delicate way.<br /><br />Be prepared for a good cry. But it's so worth it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8342077367382869081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_23032577" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23032577" />
    <a title="Kirsty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/904493-kirsty"><img alt="Kirsty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540240669p2/904493.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23032577?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kirsty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kirsty" href="/user/show/904493-kirsty">Kirsty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781862304871" href="/book/show/2327182.Before_I_Die">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23032577" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18118703983296612836">I read this in a day - I couldn't put it down. The story is told from the viewpoint of a 16 year old girl, Tessa, who has terminal leukemia. She has months to live and has made a list of things she wants to do before she dies.<br/><br/>The book is beautifully written, and brings about a number of emotions. The characters are well established (Tessa's father particularly) and this makes the story realistic and believable. It's interesting to learn about the relationships between the characters - you'd imag</span>
  <span id="freeText18118703983296612836" style="display:none">I read this in a day - I couldn't put it down. The story is told from the viewpoint of a 16 year old girl, Tessa, who has terminal leukemia. She has months to live and has made a list of things she wants to do before she dies.<br /><br />The book is beautifully written, and brings about a number of emotions. The characters are well established (Tessa's father particularly) and this makes the story realistic and believable. It's interesting to learn about the relationships between the characters - you'd imagine that most kids would turn to their parents in a situation like this, however Tessa has a slight resentment towards her father - she thinks he's holding her back and being too overprotective. <br /><br />I felt that the book captured Tessa's emotions well - she's dying, yet she refuses to let that stop her doing what she wants to do. She's very selfish at times, but then I suppose in this situation who wouldn't be at some point? She's not scared of death (most of the time) and just wants to get on with enjoying the rest of the time she has left. I thought the relationship with Adam was well written, and developed beautifully.<br /><br />Even though I knew what the ending would be, it still didn't stop me blubbing through the last 20 pages or so. I became really attached to Tessa, and it broke my heart when she died, but I loved the way in which it was written - it seemed to capture so many of Tessa's emotions.<br /><br />I chose to read this book because I like authors who deal with subjects that others are afraid to touch. Jenny Downham has done a wonderful job and I hope there are more books like this to come. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18118703983296612836" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_144191146" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144191146" />
    <a title="altough2008" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4877553-altough2008"><img alt="altough2008" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548591320p2/4877553.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144191146?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="altough2008" class="user" itemprop="url" name="altough2008" href="/user/show/4877553-altough2008">altough2008</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781862304871" href="/book/show/2327182.Before_I_Die">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4877553-altough2008?shelf=contemporary-ya">contemporary-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4877553-altough2008?shelf=book-to-movie">book-to-movie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4877553-altough2008?shelf=debut">debut</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144191146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16803737043426732872">So what was good about <i>Before I Die</i> ? I can answer in one word: Nothing.<br/><br/>Yes, Yes, I know many people have been praising this book to death, and believe me; no one is more disappointed than I am.<br/><br/>I was very excited for this book. I thought it was gonna be heartbreaking and thought-provoking. I thought it would make me appreciate life more. Boy was I wrong!<br/><br/>As a start, none of the characters appealed to me. The main character Tessa annoyed the hell out of me! I truly tried to sympathize with her, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText16803737043426732872" style="display:none">So what was good about <i>Before I Die</i> ? I can answer in one word: Nothing.<br /><br />Yes, Yes, I know many people have been praising this book to death, and believe me; no one is more disappointed than I am.<br /><br />I was very excited for this book. I thought it was gonna be heartbreaking and thought-provoking. I thought it would make me appreciate life more. Boy was I wrong!<br /><br />As a start, none of the characters appealed to me. The main character Tessa annoyed the hell out of me! I truly tried to sympathize with her, but throughout the story, there was nothing that made me feel sorry for her. In fact, I felt sorry more for the other characters who had to deal with her stupidity and insanity. Her list was stupid. I mean, breaking the law? doing drugs? I have no problem with people doing lists of things they want to do, but it has to make some significance to their character. It was never explained why she wanted do the things on her list.<br /><br />Tessa's list, or at least half of it is about doing reckless and irresponsible things. To me, Tessa seemed to think that living your life is about being wild. She continues to prove that to me until the very end. Don't get me wrong. Everybody should have fun from time to time, but you also need to be responsible if you wanna get through life. I know that Tessa doesn't have that much time left, but when you're dying, you should live your life to its fullest, not doing things that could lead to your destruction. Again, I would've sympathize with Tessa if her actions were explained, but they never were. Tessa thought she could do whatever she wants and everybody would forgive her because she was dying. Guess what? Life doesn't work that way. Believe me, I wasn't expecting Tessa to be a likable or an inspiring character. But just because a character isn't likable doesn't mean they can't be well-developed and interesting. Tessa was the exact opposite.<br /><br />However, Tessa wasn't the worst character. Oh no. The worst character was Zoey, the so called "best friend". She is easily is one of the most frustrating, weakly developed, disagreeable character I had the displeasure of reading.I never understood how these two could be friends. Tessa seemed very pathetic to me whenever she misses hanging out with Zoey who is constantly being mean to her. Zoey seemed forced to hang out with Tessa. Why? It was never explained. You don't get enough background on the character of Zoey. I could rant on and on why I hate this character, but then this review would've been much longer.<br /><br />I don't have much to say about the other characters. In general, they all seem pathetic to me. None of them is well developed due to the fact they're not given much to do, in my opinion. ALL the characters in this book didn't feel real.<br /><br />And about the love story, it happened out of nowhere! The love interest Adam has no personality. Most of the conversations between Tessa and Adam revolves around "making love" it got so annoying. I would never ever understand how or why Adam fell in love with her. I just didn't buy the "love" that was between these two. "They fell in love. How? It just happened"? As far as I know, love doesn't work that way. I love well-developed romances, but this one wasn't a love story. It was a story of lust.<br /><br />The story itself was all over the place. The chapters feel like episodes with each one tells different incident revolves around Tessa's stupid list. We follow Tessa as she tries to complete the things she wants to do before she dies, but the list is so uninteresting and idiotic that you just don't care. I'm not saying she should try doing extraordinary things like saving the world or anything, but doing drugs? seriously!? Tessa was the driving force of the plot, so that would explain why I didn't like the plot.<br /><br />I wasn't asking for an inspiring story or a likable main character when I was reading <i>Before I Die</i> . Like many people, I thought this book would be depressing. However, it didn't make me depressed at all. It made me angry. I'm sorry I'm being too harsh, but this is just my opinion. In the end, I wouldn't say don't read this book. Many people love it, so maybe there is something that I failed to see.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16803737043426732872" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('A69JuzveYizWmw0SGJvTnJojj1WQHA1kKmtRXyut3iI5iSBpgICrRHGwuXPvbtlDTHxonV6RgwNxFRfu5u4suA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1NxtZp8wEFLiaXS3wBNi3Dg8ClrHGzaBCOHTVczMi67u+gS0JG7ZOkVCwNY35mgD7mPtkgmWuOZTn5XkAY95NA==')})
  }

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_1237574').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_1237574').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_1237574').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6190139415883626652">Jenny Downham (born 1964) is a British novelist and an ex-actor. In her first book, Before I Die, the fictional account of the last few months of a sixteen-year-old girl who has been dying of leukemia for 4 years. The book is told in the first person. The book was acclaimed and was short-listed for the 2007 Guardian Award and the 2008 Lancashire Children's Book of the Year, nominated for the 2008 </span>
  <span id="freeText6190139415883626652" style="display:none">Jenny Downham (born 1964) is a British novelist and an ex-actor. In her first book, Before I Die, the fictional account of the last few months of a sixteen-year-old girl who has been dying of leukemia for 4 years. The book is told in the first person. The book was acclaimed and was short-listed for the 2007 Guardian Award and the 2008 Lancashire Children's Book of the Year, nominated for the 2008 Carnegie Medal and the 2008 Booktrust Teenage Prize, and won the 2008 Branford Boase Award.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6190139415883626652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
